[<foreign lang="ar">تزيّن</foreign> is said of language, as meaning <hi rend="ital">It was embellished, dressed up,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">trimmed:</hi> and of an action &amp;c., as meaning <hi rend="ital">it was embellished,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dressed up,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">commended,</hi> to a person, by another man, and, more commonly, by the Devil.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">تزيّن</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">He adorned, ornamented, decorated, decked,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">himself.</hi> (MA, KL.)                   </form> [as an inf. n., and also as a simple subst.,] is the <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَيْنٌ</foreign>: (S, Msb, K:) [as a simple subst.,] <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زِينَةٌ</foreign>, q. v.: (Har p. 139:) [and commonly signifying <hi rend="ital">A grace; a beauty; a comely quality; a physical,</hi> and also <hi rend="ital">an intel-lectual, adornment; an honour,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a credit;</hi> and anything that is the <hi rend="ital">pride,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">glory,</hi> of a person or thing: in these senses contr. of <foreign lang="ar">شَيْنٌ</foreign>:] pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَزْيَانٌ</foreign>. (K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Az says, I heard a boy of [the tribe called] Benoo- 'Okeyl say to another, <foreign lang="ar">وَجْهِى زَيْنٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَوَجْهُكَ شَيْنٌ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">My face is comely and thy face is ugly;</hi> for <foreign lang="ar">وَجْهِى ذُو زَيْنٍ وَوَجْهُكَ ذُو شَيْنٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">my face is possessed of comeliness and thy face is possessed of ugliness</hi>]; using the inf. ns. as epithets; like as one says <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ صَوْمٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَدْلٌ</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also The <hi rend="ital">comb</hi> of the cock. (S.)    </entryFree>28:T11cf,<entryFree id="n18543" key="زِينَةٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">زِينَةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, the subst. from <foreign lang="ar">زَانَهُ</foreign>, (Msb,) signifies <foreign lang="ar">مَا يُتَزَيَّنُ بِهِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">A thing with which,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by which, one is adorned, ornamented, decorated, decked, bedecked, garnished, embellished, beautified,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">graced;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with which,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by which, one adorns,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">himself</hi>]; (T, S, K;) <hi rend="ital">any such thing;</hi> (T, TA;) [<hi rend="ital">any ornament, ornature, decoration, garnish, embellishment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">grace;</hi>] and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n18543-1" target="زِيانٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (K;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n18543-2" target="زَيْنٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n18541"/></foreign>, also, [which see above,] signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">زِينَةٌ</foreign>: (Har p. 139:) accord. to El- Harállee, <foreign lang="ar">زِينَةٌ</foreign> denotes the [<hi rend="ital">means of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">beautifying,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">embellishing, a thing by another thing; consisting of apparel,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an ornament of gold</hi> or <hi rend="ital">silver</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of jewels</hi> or <hi rend="ital">gems,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">aspect:</hi> or, as some say, it is the <hi rend="ital">beauty</hi> [<hi rend="ital">seen</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of the eye that does not reach to the interior of that which is adorned</hi> [<hi rend="ital">thereby</hi>]: accord. to Er-Rághib, its proper mean- <pb n="1280"/> ing is <hi rend="ital">a thing that does not disgrace,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">render unseemly, a man, in any of his states</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conditions, either in the present world or in that which is to come:</hi> but that which adorns him in one state or condition, exclusively of another, is in one point of view <foreign lang="ar">شَيْنٌ</foreign>: summarily speaking, it is of three kinds; namely, <hi rend="ital">mental, such as knowledge</hi> or <hi rend="ital">science, and good tenets;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">bodily, such as strength, and tallness of stature, and beauty of aspect;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">extrinsic, such as wealth, and rank</hi> or <hi rend="ital">station</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dignity;</hi> and all these are mentioned in the Kur: (TA:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">زِيَنٌ</foreign>. (Bd in x. 25.) <foreign lang="ar">زِينَةُ الحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا</foreign> [or simply <foreign lang="ar">زِينَةُ الدُّنْيَا</foreign> generally means <hi rend="ital">The ornature, finery, show, pomp,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">gaiety, of the present life</hi> or <hi rend="ital">world;</hi> and] particularly includes <hi rend="ital">wealth and children.</hi> (Kur xviii. 44.) <foreign lang="ar">زِينَةُ الأَرْضِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The ornature of the earth</hi>] means <hi rend="ital">the plants,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">herbage, of the earth.</hi> (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ الزِّينَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The day of ornature</hi>] is <hi rend="ital">the festival</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">العِيدُ</foreign>); (S, K;) when men used [and still use] to adorn themselves with goodly articles of apparel. (TA.) And also <hi rend="ital">The day of the breaking</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of the dam a little within the entrance</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of the canal of Misr</hi> [here meaning the present capital of Egypt, El-Káhireh, which we call “ Cairo ”], (K, TA,) i. e. the canal which runs through the midst of Misr, and [the dam of] which is broken when the Nile has attained the height of sixteen cubits or more: this day is said to be meant in the Kur xx. 61: it is one of the days observed in Egypt with the greatest gladness and rejoicing from ancient times; and its observance in the days of the Fátimees was such as is inconceivable, as it is described in the “ Khitat ” of El-Makreezee. (TA. [The modern observances of this day, and of other days in relation to the rise of the Nile, are described in my work on the Modern Egyptians.])    </entryFree>29:Tb94,<entryFree id="n18553" key="مُتَزَيِّنٌ" type="main">

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n18553-3" target="مُزَيَّنٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n18548"/></foreign>: and the first signifies also <hi rend="ital">selfadorned</hi> &amp;c.]: (TA:) the second and third are part. ns. of <foreign lang="ar">اِزْدَانَ</foreign>; the third being formed from the second by incorporation [of the <foreign lang="ar">د</foreign> into the <foreign lang="ar">ز</foreign>]: and the dim. of <foreign lang="ar">مُزْدَانٌ</foreign> is
